Joint Kitabah, Miscarriage, and Ownership Disputes (Al-Muhit & Al-Mabsut Cases)
Covers three ancillary cases: joint kitabah with umm walad, miscarriage, and ownership disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply rulings from al-Muhit and al-Mabsut to cases of joint kitabah, miscarriage after pregnancy claim, and conflicting ownership claims regarding a mukatabah umm walad.

Core Idea
In joint kitabah, one slave becoming umm walad does not void the contract; a miscarriage after pregnancy claim brings ghurrah; ownership claims are rejected after umm walad status is established.

This lesson extracts three specific case rulings from the authoritative works al-Muhit and al-Mabsut, showing how the Hanafi school handles nuanced situations. First, when two slaves are contracted as a single kitabah and one becomes an umm walad, the contract remains intact for both because they cannot be separated. Second, if a master claims pregnancy and a third party causes a miscarriage, the ghurrah (blood money for the fetus) goes to the father (master), and the mother can take compensation (uqr) if she continues the kitabah. Third, if the master later acknowledges that the mukatabah belongs to another, his acknowledgment is invalid because her status as umm walad is established and cannot be undone by their agreement.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the joint kitabah case
A man contracts kitabah with two slave girls as one unit. One then has a child by the master, making her an umm walad. The child is free, but she remains a mukatabah. She cannot unilaterally void the kitabah because the contract is indivisible.
The text: 'she has no option because she cannot be returned to slavery without the other.'
2
Understand the daughter's status
If one maid gives birth to a daughter, and the master later has a child by that daughter, the daughter becomes umm walad for the master. She cannot declare incapacity (ta'jiz) because she is dependent on her mother's contract.
The daughter is considered a dependent of the mother in the joint kitabah.
3
Miscarriage after claim of pregnancy
If the master claims the mukatabah is pregnant and a third party strikes her causing miscarriage, the ghurrah is paid to the master (father). The mother does not inherit from the fetus, but can take uqr (compensation for injury) if she chooses to continue the kitabah.
Ghurrah: a fixed compensation for a fetus.
4
Acknowledgment of ownership dispute
If the master acknowledges that the mukatabah is actually a slave of another (claimant), this acknowledgment is not accepted because her status as umm walad is already established. The claimant's assertion must be proven otherwise.
The text: 'they are not believed in voiding it' – the right of umm walad is protected.

Source Text

المحيط : رجل كاتب جاريتين مكاتبة واحدة ثم استولد أحدهما فالولد حر والأم مكاتبة كما كانت ولا خيار لها لأن الاستيلاد حصل في ملكه فعلق حراً. وإنما قلنا لا خيار لها لأنه لا يمكن ردها إلى الرق بدون الأخرى، ولو ولدت إحداهما بنتاً فاستولد المولى البنت صارت أم ولد له والولد حر بغير القيمة ، وليس لها أن تعجز نفسها وتبطل الكتابة لأنها تابعة لأمها وإذا تعذر فسخ الكتابة تصير أم ولد له .اهـ. فلو قال بعقد مفرد لسلم. وفي المبسوط : إذا ادعى المولى حبل المكاتبة فضرب إنسان بطنها بعد ذلك فألقت جنيناً ميتاً فإن في الولد غرة لأبيه لأنه عتق بيوم بدعوته فكان ميراثاً له ولا ترث شيئاً ولكنها تأخذ العقر إن اختارت المضي على المكاتبة اهـ . فلو قال ولو ادعى جبلها فضرب آخر بطنها فألقت جنيناً ميتاً مضت إلى آخره. لكان أولى لأنه يعلم حكم ما إذا ولدته فادعاه بالأولى. وفي المبسوط أيضاً : ولدت مكاتبة من مولاها ثم أقر المولى أنها أمة لفلان لم يصدق وإن صدقته في ذلك لأن حق أمومية الولد قد ثبت لها فلا يصدقان في إبطالها. فإن قال المدعي بعتها منك بألف ولم ينقد الثمن وقال المولى زوجتني والأمة معروفة للمدعي فعلى المولى المهر لمستوفيه قصاصاً من الثمن، وليس عليه قيمة في الأم ولا في الولد وإن لم تكن معروفة أنها للمدعي ضمن القيمة ألا ترى أنه لو أنكر البيع لم يتمكن من استردادها فيضمن قيمتها بعد أن يحلف بالله ما اشتراها منه بما يدعيه من الثمن اهـ. وقيد بقوله «مكاتبة من سيدها ليحترز عن أمة المكاتب فإن صدقه ثبت النسب ويضمن قيمة الولد وتعتبر قيمته يوم الولادة هذا إذا جاءت به لستة أشهر من حين اشتراها، فلو جاءت به لأقل فادعاه المولى لا تصح دعوته، وكذا إذا اشترى المكاتب غلاماً من السوق لا تصح دعوته إلا بتصديق المكاتب عبد كاتبه وكاتب العبد أمة ثم ولدت المكاتبة ولداً فادعاه مولى المكاتب فالمسألة على وجوه إما إن صدقاه في ذلك أو كذباه أو صدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر، فإن جاءت بالولد لستة أشهر فأكثر فصدقاه في ذلك أو صدقه المكاتب ثبت النسب منه، وإن كذباه في ذلك أو كذبته المكاتبة لا يثبت النسب والعبرة هنا بتصديق المكاتبة دون المكاتب
Book of the Mukatab, Chapter on what is permissible for the mukatab to do and what is not. It is dissolved (the contract) with respect to the compensation and remains with respect to earning and children, because dissolution is for their benefit, and the benefit is as we mentioned. And if she dies and leaves wealth, her kitabah is paid from it, and what remains is inheritance for her child, because her freedom is established in the last part of her life. And if she leaves no wealth, then there is no sa'y upon the child because he is free. And if she gives birth to another child, his lineage is not established without a claim, because intercourse with her is prohibited. And the child of an umm walad is only established in lineage without a claim if her intercourse was lawful. And if she rendered herself incapable and gave birth after that to a child within a period in which conception after ta'jiz is possible, his lineage is established without a claim, unless he explicitly disowns him. And if he does not claim the second child and she dies without paying, this child performs sa'y for the kitabah compensation because he is a mukatab as a dependent of her. And if the master dies after that, he becomes free and the sa'y is dropped from him because he is like an umm walad. And he (the author) said generally 'mukatabah' so it includes whether she is alone in the contract or with another, and what he mentioned is specific to the first. He said in al-Muhit: A man contracts kitabah with two slave girls as one kitabah, then he has a child by one of them, then the child is free and the mother remains a mukatabah as before, and she has no option, because istilad occurred in his ownership, so it is attached to freedom. We say she has no option because she cannot be returned to slavery without the other. And if one of them gives birth to a daughter and the master has a child by the daughter, she becomes umm walad for him, and the child is free without value, and she cannot declare herself incapable and void the kitabah because she is dependent on her mother, and if voiding the kitabah is not possible, she becomes umm walad for him. End. So if he said by a single contract, it is sound. And in al-Mabsut: If the master claims pregnancy of the mukatabah, then a person strikes her belly after that and she miscarries a dead fetus, then for the child is a ghurrah paid to the father because he became free by the day of his claim, so it is inheritance for him, and she does not inherit anything, but she takes the compensation if she chooses to proceed with the kitabah. End. So if he said: 'and if he claimed her pregnancy and another struck her belly and she miscarried a dead fetus, she proceeds' to the rest, it would be more appropriate because it informs the ruling if she gave birth and he claimed it. And in al-Mabsut also: A mukatabah gives birth from her master, then the master acknowledges that she is a slave of so-and-so, he is not believed even if she confirms him, because the right of umm walad of the child has been established for her, so they are not believed in voiding it. So if the claimant says, 'I sold her to you for a thousand and you did not pay the price,' and the master says, 'You married her to me,' and the slave is known to be the claimant's, then the master owes the dower to the one who received it in exchange from the price, and he is not liable for the value of the mother or the child. And if it is not known that she belongs to the claimant, he guarantees the value. Do you not see that if he denies the sale, he cannot retrieve her, so he guarantees her value after swearing by Allah that he did not buy her from him for the price he claims. End. And he restricted by his word 'mukatabah from her master' to exclude the slave of a mukatab, for if he confirms him, lineage is established and he guarantees the value of the child, and its value is considered on the day of birth, provided she gave birth at six months from the time he bought her. If she gave birth in less time and the master claims, his claim is not valid. Likewise, if the mukatab buys a boy from the market, his claim is not valid except with confirmation of the mukatab. A slave contracts kitabah with the mukatab, and the mukatab's slave is an umm walad, then she gives birth, and the master of the mukatab claims the child. The case has aspects: either both of them confirm him, or both deny him, or one confirms and the other denies. If she gave birth at six months or more and they both confirm or the mukatab confirms, lineage is established. If they deny or the mukatabah denies, lineage is not established. And the criterion here is the confirmation of the mukatabah, not the mukatab.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings regarding a female slave who is both a mukatabah (contracted to earn her freedom) and an umm walad (mother of her master's child). The author explains that if this mukatabah dies, her freedom is considered to have occurred at the last moment of her life, so any remaining wealth after paying her kitabah becomes inheritance for her child. If she dies insolvent, the child is free and owes nothing. The text then addresses lineage for a child born after the contract: if she gives birth to another child, his lineage is not automatically established because intercourse is prohibited. Only for a child born from lawful intercourse (like the umm walad's) is lineage fixed without claim. However, if she declares herself incapable (ta'jiz) and then gives birth within a possible conception period, the child's lineage is established unless the master explicitly disowns him. If the master does not claim the second child and she dies without paying, that child must perform sa'y (work to pay off the kitabah debt) as a dependent mukatab. But if the master dies, the child is freed like an umm walad's child. The quote from al-Muhit illustrates an edge case: if a master contracts kitabah with two maids as one unit and then has a child by one, the child is free but the mother remains a mukatabah. She cannot opt out because the contract cannot be voided for one without the other. The quote from al-Mabsut covers a scenario where the master claims pregnancy and a third party causes a miscarriage; the ghurrah is paid to the father. Lastly, the text discusses claims of ownership and lineage when a third party asserts ownership of the mukatabah after she has given birth. The authorities emphasize that once she is established as an umm walad, later claims are not entertained without evidence. The final part deals with distinguishing between a mukatabah owned by the master versus a slave of a mukatab, where lineage rules differ.

Key Terms
غرّة (ghurrah): A fixed compensation for the loss of a fetus, paid to the father.
عقر (uqr): Compensation paid to a female slave for unlawful intercourse or injury, here for the assault causing miscarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the al-Muhit case, why can't the maid who becomes umm walad opt out of the joint kitabah?
A) She consents to stay.
B) She cannot be freed without the other.
C) The master forbids it.
D) The kitabah is already dissolved.

Key Takeaway
Joint kitabah is indivisible; a miscarriage after claim gives ghurrah to the father; ownership claims are invalid after umm walad status is established.

Kitabah of Umm Walad and Mudabbar: Validity and Death Effects
Expansion on kitabah validity and post-death effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of kitabah for umm walad and mudabbar, and identify the different positions on the mudabbar's obligation upon the master's death.

Core Idea
Kitabah with umm walad and mudabbar is valid; at death, umm walad is freed gratis, mudabbar has options.

This lesson expands on two related rulings from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. First, the validity of contracting kitabah with an umm walad or a mudabbar is established despite their special status. Second, when the master dies, the consequences differ: the umm walad is freed automatically, while the mudabbar must pay a portion. The intra-Hanafi disagreement on the mudabbar's obligation reveals a deeper principle about the divisibility of emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special statuses
Recognize that umm walad (mother of the master's child) and mudabbar (slave promised freedom after death) have partially free statuses. Understand that their ownership is still respected, making kitabah valid.
Umm walad is not fully property (ghayr mutaqawwima) but still owned.
2
Understand the proof for validity
The author argues that the master's ownership in both is established, even if the umm walad is not marketable. Taking compensation for freedom is like qisas (blood money) — it's a recognized exchange.
Dalil aqli: ownership respected leads to validity of contract.
3
Analyze the effect of master's death on umm walad
Upon death, the umm walad is freed automatically (by istilad) and her kitabah debt is voided. Any earnings she made before death belong to her, not the master's estate.
Freedom from two sources: kitabah and istilad; the stronger (istilad) prevails.
4
Analyze the effect on mudabbar and the ikhtilaf
The mudabbar, being partially free (one-third at death), faces two obligations: the remaining kitabah debt and the sa'y for the freed portion. The three Hanafi imams differ on his choice and the amount.
Abu Hanifa: option; Abu Yusuf: lesser of value or debt; Muhammad: lesser of two-thirds of value or two-thirds of debt.
5
Connect to the principle of tajazzi' al-i'taq
The dispute centers on whether emancipation is divisible. Abu Hanifa says yes, so the mudabbar remains partly slave and his kitabah continues; the others imply limits on divisibility.
This principle affects many rulings on partial freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن كاتب أم ولده أو مدبره صح لأن ملكه ثابت في كل واحد منهما وإن كانت أم الولد غير متقومة عند الإمام وعقد إثبات هذه المكاتبة لها بالبدل ولأن ملكه فيها محترم وإن لم يكن متقوماً عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، فكان أخذ العوض عنه كالقصاص وعقد الكتابة ليرد على المملوك لحاجته إلى التوصل إلى ملك السيد في والحرية في المآل وأمر الولد في هذا لغيرها لأنها مملوكة يداً ورقبة فإنها تملك ما يملكه المكاتب في الحال والمآل وكسبها للولي. قال في الهداية ولا تنافي بينهما لأنها تلقاها جهتا حرية . قال صاحب الغياثية : لا يقال أحدهما يقتضي العتق ببدل والآخر بلا بدل والعتق لا يثبت لهما فكانا متنافيين لأنا نقول : لا تنافي بينهما لكونهما جهتي عتق تلقاها على سبيل البدل، وعورض بأنه إن أراد الوحدة الشخصية غير مسلم كيف وفي العتق بالكتابة تسلم لها الاكساب؟ وإن أراد النوعية فلا تنافي. وفي المحيط ومن كاتب أم ولده على خدمتها أو رقبتها جاز فأراد بقوله على خدمتها ورقبتها أن تصير أحق بخدمتها أو رقبتها بأن كاتبها بألف على أن تصير أحق بخدمتها أو برقبتها فهو الصحيح لأن ذكر الخدمة بدون المدة لا يصح . وكذا الرقبة لا يتصور أن تكون بدلاً لأن الشيء الواحد لا يصلح أن يكون بدلاً ومبدلاً، ولو وطئها بعدما كاتبها يجب العقر لأن العقر والأرش بمنزلة الكسب . قال رحمه الله : (وعتقت مجاناً بموته) أي عتقت بموت المولى بغير شيء يلزمها وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة لأنها عتقت بالاستيلاد وتسلم لها الأولاد والاكساب لأنها عتقت وهي مكاتبة وملكه يمنع من ثبوت ملك الغير فصار فيه كما إذا أعتقها المولى في حال حياته، ولئن انفسخت الكتابة في حقها بقيت الحرية في حق الأولاد والأكساب لأن الفسخ للنظر والنظر فيما ذكرنا. ولو أدت البدل قبل موت المولى عتقت بالكتابة كبقائها إلى وقت الأداء، وبالأداء تقرر ولا يبطل. قال صاحب غاية البيان : ولقائل أن يقول : النظر في إيفاء حقها وحقها حصل لا في إبطال حق الغير لأن الكسب حصل لها قبل موت المولى وكلامنا فيه ولم يعتق قبل موت المولى بل حينئذ فينبغي أن يكون الكسب للمولى لا لها . قال رحمه الله : ( وسعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته أو كل البدل بموته فقيراً) يعني لو مات من كاتبه ولا مال له غيره فهو بالخيار أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو جميع بدل الكتابة وهذا عند الإمام. وقال الثاني : يسعى في الأقل منهما. وقال الثالث: يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي قيمته وثلثي بدل الكتابة فالخلاف في الموضعين في الخيار وفي المقدار، وأبو يوسف مع أبي حنيفة مع المقدار ومع محمد في نفي الخيار والكلام في الخيار مبني على تجزئ الإعتاق وعدمه، فعنده لما كان متجزئاً بقي ما وراء الثلث عبداً وبقيت الكتابة فيه كما كانت قبل عتق الثلث فتوجه لعتقه جهتان كتابة مؤجلة وسعاية معجلة فيتخير للتفاوت بين
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he contracts kitabah with his umm walad or his mudabbar, it is valid, because his ownership is established in each of them, even though the umm walad is not considered property (ghayr mutaqawwima) according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the contract of proving this kitabah for her is by compensation, and because his ownership in her is respected, even if it is not considered property according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be exalted. So taking compensation for it is like qisas. And the kitabah contract is to return (the slave) to the master's ownership in the present and freedom in the future. And the matter of the child in this is for other than her, because she is owned in hand and neck (full ownership). So she owns what the mukatab owns in the present and future, and her earning is for her master. He said in al-Hidayah: There is no conflict between them (kitabah and istilad) because she encounters two aspects of freedom. The author of al-Ghiyathiyyah said: It cannot be said that one requires freedom with compensation and the other without compensation, and freedom cannot be established for two (contradictory) causes, so they are contradictory. Because we say: There is no conflict between them because they are two aspects of freedom that she encounters on the basis of substitution. And it was objected: If he means personal unity (of the two freedoms), it is not accepted, for in freedom by kitabah her earnings are given to her? And if he means generic unity, then there is no conflict. And in al-Muhit: And whoever contracts kitabah with his umm walad for her service or her substance, it is valid. So by his words 'for her service or her substance' he means that she becomes entitled to her service or her substance, as if he contracts kitabah with her for a thousand on condition that she becomes entitled to her service or substance. This is the correct view because mentioning service without a term is invalid. Likewise, substance cannot be imagined as a substitute, because one thing cannot be a substitute and a thing substituted. And if he has intercourse with her after contracting kitabah, he must pay the compensation (uqr) because uqr and compensation for injury are like earnings (which belong to the master). He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And she is freed gratis upon his death) meaning she becomes free upon the master's death without anything being required of her, and the kitabah compensation is dropped from her, because she is freed by istilad. And the children and earnings are given to her, because she was freed while being a mukatabah, and his (the master's) ownership prevents the establishment of another's ownership, so it becomes like if the master freed her during his life. And if the kitabah is dissolved with respect to her, freedom remains with respect to the children and earnings, because dissolution is for their benefit, and the benefit is what we mentioned. And if she pays the compensation before the master's death, she is freed by the kitabah, as if she continued until the time of payment, and it is established and does not void. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan said: Some may say: Consideration is for fulfilling her right, and her right has been obtained, not for voiding another's right. Because the earning accrued to her before the master's death, and our discourse is about it, and she did not become free before the master's death but at that moment. So it should be that the earning belongs to the master, not to her. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the mudabbar performs sa'y for two-thirds of his value or the entire compensation upon his death if he is poor), meaning if the master from whom he contracted kitabah dies and has no other property, then the mudabbar has the option to perform sa'y for two-thirds of his value or for the entire kitabah debt. This is according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the second (Abu Yusuf) said: he performs sa'y for the lesser of the two. And the third (Muhammad) said: he performs sa'y for the lesser of two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitabah debt. So the disagreement is in both the option and the amount. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa in amount and with Muhammad in negation of the option. And the discussion on the option is based on the divisibility of manumission. For him (Abu Hanifa), since it is divisible, what remains beyond one-third remains a slave, and the kitabah continues in it as before the emancipation of one-third. So two aspects become binding for his emancipation: deferred kitabah and immediate sa'y, so he chooses between the two due to the difference.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on two rulings from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. First, the author validates the kitabah of an umm walad and a mudabbar, countering the objection that an umm walad is not considered property (ghayr mutaqawwima) according to Abu Hanifa. The reasoning is that while she may not have a market value, her master's ownership is nonetheless respected, and taking compensation for her freedom is analogous to taking blood-money (qisas). The commentary from al-Hidayah and al-Ghiyathiyyah addresses a potential conflict: how can the same slave be freed by kitabah (with payment) and by istilad (without payment)? The answer is that these are two distinct aspects (jihaat) of freedom; they are not contradictory because they apply to different situations. The text then discusses the rules for kitabah on service or substance (al-khidma wa al-raqaba), clarifying that it is valid only if the service is specified for a term. The second ruling concerns the effect of the master's death on the umm walad and the mudabbar. The umm walad is freed automatically and her kitabah is voided, while the mudabbar has a choice: he can either pay two-thirds of his value (since one-third of his value is already freed as tadbir) or pay the full kitabah debt. The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is detailed: Abu Hanifa gives him the choice, Abu Yusuf requires the lesser of the two amounts, and Muhammad requires the lesser of two-thirds of the value or two-thirds of the debt. The basis of the disagreement is the divisibility of emancipation (tajazzi' al-i'taq): Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation is divisible, so only one-third of the mudabbar's value is freed at death, leaving the rest subject to the kitabah contract. The full text of the last sentence is cut off but implies that the slave can choose the easier option.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, entitling her to freedom upon his death.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared 'you are free after my death' (tadbir), making him automatically free upon the master's death from one-third of his value.
تجزئ الإعتاق (tajazzi' al-i'taq): The concept that the emancipation of a slave can be divisible, meaning part of him can be free while part remains slave.
سعاية (sa'y): Work performed by a slave or mukatab to earn money to pay a debt for freedom or compensation.
جاهتا حرية (jihata hurriyya): Two aspects of freedom: in this context, the umm walad encounters two paths to freedom—by kitabah and by istilad—which are not contradictory because they apply to different situations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is kitabah with an umm walad valid even though she is not considered property (ghayr mutaqawwima)?
A) Because she is fully owned like any other slave.
B) Because the master's ownership in her is respected, and taking compensation is like qisas.
C) Because the umm walad is not a slave at all.
D) Because the child's freedom depends on it.

Key Takeaway
Kitabah with umm walad and mudabbar is valid; upon the master's death, the umm walad is freed gratis, while the mudabbar has an option to pay two-thirds of his value or the full kitabah debt.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Mudabbir's Obligation After Master's Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the mudabbir's obligation after master's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on the mudabbir's obligation when the master dies insolvent, and explain the basis of their disagreement on the divisibility of emancipation.

Core Idea
The mudabbir's kitabah creates a conflict; Abu Hanifa allows choice, Sahibayn do not.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its sharh addresses a delicate intra-Hanafi dispute about what happens when a master who has made kitabah with his mudabbir dies insolvent. The mudabbir faces two obligations: the deferred kitabah price and the immediate service for the freed portion. The three imams differ on whether he has a choice and on the exact amount he must pay. Understanding the principle of divisibility of emancipation is key to grasping the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The master makes a kitabah contract with his mudabbir, then dies with no other property. The mudabbir is now partially free by tadbir (one-third) and partially a mukatab. Determine what the mudabbir owes.
The mudabbir's freedom is deferred, so upon death one-third becomes free immediately.
2
State the three positions
Abu Hanifa: the mudabbir may choose to serve for two-thirds of his value or pay the full kitabah price. Abu Yusuf: he must serve for the lesser of the two. Muhammad: he must serve for the lesser of two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitabah price.
The difference is in both choice and amount.
3
Analyze the basis of disagreement
Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation is divisible (mutajazzi'), so after one-third is freed, the remaining two-thirds is still a slave with kitabah intact, creating two obligations. The Sahibayn hold emancipation is not divisible, so when one-third is freed, the entire slave becomes free and the kitabah dissolves, leaving only the service obligation for two-thirds of the value.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) about the nature of emancipation.
4
Identify the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf is the amount the mudabbir pays. For example, if the kitabah price is 1000 and the value is 1200, Abu Hanifa gives a choice between 800 and 1000; Abu Yusuf requires 800; Muhammad requires 666.67.
The mufta bihi is not specified in this passage.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب باب ما يجوز للمكاتب أن يفعله وما لا يجوز قال رحمه الله : (وإن كاتب أم ولده أو مدبره صح لأن ملكه ثابت في كل واحد منهما وإن كانت أم الولد غير متقومة عند الإمام وعقد إثبات هذه المكاتبة لها بالبدل ولأن ملكه فيها محترم وإن لم يكن متقوماً عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، فكان أخذ العوض عنه كالقصاص وعقد الكتابة ليرد على المملوك لحاجته إلى التوصل إلى ملك السيد في والحرية في المآل وأمر الولد في وقت الأداء، وبالأداء تقرر ولا يبطل. قال صاحب غاية البيان : ولقائل أن يقول : النظر في إيفاء حقها وحقها حصل لا في إبطال حق الغير لأن الكسب حصل لها قبل موت المولى وكلامنا فيه ولم يعتق قبل موت المولى بل حينئذ فينبغي أن يكون الكسب للمولى لا لها . قال رحمه الله : ( وسعى المدبر في ثلثي قيمته أو كل البدل بموته فقيراً) يعني لو مات من كاتبه ولا مال له غيره فهو بالخيار أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو جميع بدل الكتابة وهذا عند الإمام. وقال الثاني : يسعى في الأقل منهما. وقال الثالث: يسعى في الأقل من ثلثي قيمته وثلثي بدل الكتابة فالخلاف في الموضعين في الخيار وفي المقدار، وأبو يوسف مع أبي حنيفة مع المقدار ومع محمد في نفي الخيار والكلام في الخيار مبني على تجزئ الإعتاق وعدمه، فعنده لما كان متجزئاً بقي ما وراء الثلث عبداً وبقيت الكتابة فيه كما كانت قبل عتق الثلث فتوجه لعتقه جهتان كتابة مؤجلة وسعاية معجلة فيتخير للتفاوت بين الأمرين. وعندهما العتق لا يتجزئ لأنه عتق كله بعتق ثلثه فبطلت لكتابة فلم يثبت الخيار، والدليل ما مر في كتاب العتق واعترض عليه بأن الإعتاق لما لم يتجزأ عندهما لما عتق ثلثه عتق كله فانفسخت الكتابة فوجبت السعاية في ثلثي قيمته لا غير وأجيب بأنا قد حكمنا بصحة الكتابة نظراً لها فيقبضاها كذلك فلربما يكون لها أقل فيحصل النظر بوجوبه لها. وأما المقدار فعندهما لا يسقط عنه من بدل الكتابة شيء، وعند محمد يسقط عنه ثلثه لأن الكتابة صادفت ثلثه وعتق ثلثه بالتدبير فيبطل ما بإزائه من البدل ولهما أن المال قوبل بما تصح مقابلته به وبما لا تصح فانصرف كله إلى ما لا تصح والتدبير يوجب استحقاق ثلث رقبته لا محالة فلا يتصور استحقاقه بالكتابة، وهذا بخلاف ما لو دبر مكاتبته لأن البدل هناك مقابل بكل الرقبة إن لم يستحق شيء من الرقبة عند الكتابة، فإذا أعتق بعض الرقبة نفذ ذلك بالتدبير وسقط حصته من بدل الكتابة بقدره أما هنا فالكتابة وقعت بعد التدبير ومالية الثلث قد سقطت فكان البدل بأداء الثلثين ضرورة وليس هذا كما إذا أدى في حياته لأن استحقاق الثلث قد سقط بالتدبير وفي المبسوط : لو كاتب عبده المأذون المديون فللغرماء بعضها لأنها تضمنت إبطال حقهم، فإذا أخذ المولى الكتابة ثم علموا فلهم أخذها من المولى لأنه كسب عبد مأذون مديون والغرماء أحق بإكسابه قبل الكتابة فكذا بعدها بخلاف ما لو ضرب على عبده المأذون المديون ضريبة مال صح وما يأخذ المولى من الضربية مسلم له لأن الضربية بدل المنفعة وللمولى أن يستوفي المنفعة بالاستخدام فكذا له الضريبة بدلاً . عنه . وإن بقي من دينهم شيء ضمن له المولى قيمته ويسعى في بقية دينهم ولا يرجع المولى على العبد بما أدى، وكذا لو قضى المولى دينهم جازت الكتابة ولم يرجع على العبد بما أدى من دينهم. أمة مأذونة في التجارة وعليها دين فولدت فكاتب السيد الولد وعتقه فللغرماء رد الكتابة وفي العتق يضمن المولى قيمة الولد.
Book of Mukatab. Chapter on what is permitted for the mukatab to do and what is not. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If he makes a kitabah with his umm walad or his mudabbir, it is valid because his ownership is established over each of them, even though the umm walad is not considered property according to Imam Abu Hanifa; and this contract establishes the kitabah for her in exchange for a payment, and because his ownership over her is respected even if not considered property according to Abu Hanifa, so taking compensation for it is like qisas. The contract of kitabah is intended to return the slave to his need to attain ownership of the master and freedom in the future. The matter of the umm walad differs from others because she is owned in hand and neck, so she owns what the mukatab owns in present and future, and her earnings belong to her guardian. He said in al-Hidayah: There is no contradiction between them (kitabah and ownership) because she receives two aspects of freedom. The author of al-Ghiyathiyyah said: It cannot be said that one (kitabah) necessitates freedom with a payment and the other (umm walad status) without payment, and freedom is not established for both, so they contradict; we say: There is no contradiction because they are two aspects of freedom that she receives alternately. It was objected: If he means personal unity, it is not granted, for in freedom through kitabah she acquires earnings? If he means generic, then there is no contradiction. In al-Muhit: If he makes a kitabah with his umm walad on her service or her neck (possession), it is valid; what is meant by 'on her service and her neck' is that she becomes entitled to her service or her neck (possession) by paying a thousand; this is correct because mentioning service without a duration is invalid. Likewise, the neck (possession) cannot be conceived as a substitute because a single thing cannot be both substitute and substituted. If he has intercourse with her after the kitabah, he must pay an indemnity because indemnity and damages are considered earnings. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And she is freed for free upon his death) meaning she is freed upon the master's death without anything being incumbent upon her, and the kitabah payment drops from her because she is freed by the birth of a child (istilad). Her children and earnings are given to her because she is freed while being a mukatabah, and his ownership prevents the establishment of ownership of another, so it is as if the master freed her during his lifetime. Even if the kitabah is dissolved concerning her, freedom remains concerning the children and earnings because dissolution is for consideration, and the consideration is what we mentioned. If she pays the payment before the master's death, she is freed by the kitabah, as it remains until the time of payment, and by payment it is confirmed and not invalidated. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan said: One might say: Consideration is in fulfilling her right, and her right is obtained, not in invalidating the right of another because the earning was obtained before the master's death, and our discussion is about that; she was not freed before the master's death, so at that time the earnings should belong to the master, not her. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the mudabbir serves for two-thirds of his value or the entire kitabah payment if the master dies insolvent) meaning if the one who made the kitabah dies and has no other property, he has a choice to serve for two-thirds of his value or the entire kitabah payment according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). The second (Abu Yusuf) said: He serves for the lesser of the two. The third (Muhammad) said: He serves for the lesser of two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitabah payment. The ikhtilaf is in two points: in the choice and in the amount. Abu Yusuf agrees with Abu Hanifa on the amount and with Muhammad on denial of choice. The discussion on choice is built on the divisibility of emancipation and its non-divisibility. According to him (Abu Hanifa), since it is divisible, what remains beyond one-third is a slave, and the kitabah remains on it as it was before the emancipation of one-third, so two aspects face him: a deferred kitabah and an immediate service, so he chooses between the two. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), emancipation is not divisible, so when one-third is freed, he becomes entirely free, and the kitabah is invalidated; thus, no choice is established. The evidence is what was mentioned in the Book of Emancipation. It was objected: Since emancipation is not divisible according to them, when one-third is freed, he becomes entirely free, the kitabah dissolves, so only service for two-thirds of his value is required. The answer: We have judged the kitabah to be valid for consideration of the slave, so they serve accordingly; perhaps the lesser (amount) may obtain consideration. As for the amount, according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), nothing is dropped from the kitabah payment; according to Muhammad, one-third is dropped because the kitabah occurred on one-third of him, and one-third is freed by tadbir, so the corresponding portion of the payment is void. Their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argument: The wealth is counterbalanced by what can be countered and by what cannot, so it all goes to what cannot be countered. Tadbir necessarily establishes entitlement to one-third of his neck, so entitlement through kitabah cannot be conceived. This is unlike if one makes tadbir of his mukatab because there the payment is counterbalanced by the entire neck if nothing of the neck was previously entitled; so if some part of the neck is freed, that takes effect by tadbir, and its share of the kitabah payment drops in proportion. Here, the kitabah occurred after tadbir, and the value of one-third has fallen, so the payment is necessarily for two-thirds. This is not like if he paid during his lifetime because the entitlement to one-third has fallen by tadbir. In al-Mabsut: If he makes a kitabah with his authorized slave who is indebted, the creditors have some right (to it) because the kitabah entails invalidating their right. If the master takes the kitabah payment and then the creditors learn, they can take it from the master because it is the earning of an authorized indebted slave, and the creditors have more right to his earnings before the kitabah and likewise after. This is unlike if he imposed a tax (dhariba) on his authorized indebted slave, which is valid; what the master takes from the tax is granted to him because the tax is a substitute for usufruct, and the master is entitled to usufruct through employment, so likewise the tax is his substitute... If some of their debt remains, the master guarantees his value, and he serves for the remaining debt, and the master does not recourse against the slave for what he paid. Likewise, if the master pays off their debt, the kitabah becomes valid, and he does not recourse against the slave for what he paid of their debt. An authorized female slave in trade with debt, who gives birth, then the master makes a kitabah with the child and frees him; the creditors can rescind the kitabah, and in the emancipation, the master guarantees the value of the child.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and commentary on the ruling of kitabah with the umm walad (mother of the master's child) and the mudabbir (slave whose freedom is deferred to the master's death). The author first states the ruling that such kitabah is valid, despite the umm walad not being considered property according to Abu Hanifa. The proof is that ownership over her is established and respected, and taking compensation is akin to qisas. The commentary then clarifies no contradiction between her two aspects of freedom (via kitabah and via umm walad status). Sub-rulings follow: kitabah on service or possession of the umm walad is valid if properly conditioned; if the master has intercourse with the mokataba, he must pay an indemnity (jabr), treated as earnings. The matn then states that the umm walad is freed gratis upon the master's death, and the kitabah payment falls off. This is because she is freed by istilad (bearing a child). Her children and earnings are hers. The commentary discusses whether earnings before death go to the master. Next, the mudabbir's obligation upon the master's death if the master is insolvent: according to Abu Hanifa, the mudabbir may choose between serving for two-thirds of his value or paying the full kitabah price; Abu Yusuf says he must serve the lesser of the two; Muhammad says he serves the lesser of two-thirds of value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. The ikhtilaf is based on whether emancipation is divisible (Abu Hanifa) or not (Sahibayn). A detailed discussion follows, including the difference between a mudabbir who is later given kitabah versus a mukatab who is later made mudabbir. Finally, the text from al-Mabsut covers cases of kitabah with an authorized indebted slave: creditors have priority over the kitabah payment because it is an earning; if the master takes it, creditors can recover it from him. There are also rulings on partial debts and freedom of the child of an authorized slave.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; she is not considered property according to Abu Hanifa but her kitabah is valid.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave whose freedom is deferred to the master's death through tadbir.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a kitabah contract to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
سعاية (sa'i): The service or payment the slave performs to earn his freedom after the master's death in the context of tadbir.
كتابة (kitabah): A contract of manumission by which a slave agrees to pay a sum to the master in exchange for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what choice does the mudabbir have if the master dies insolvent?
A) He must pay the full kitabah price.
B) He may choose to serve for two-thirds of his value or pay the entire kitabah price.
C) He must serve for two-thirds of his value only.
D) He must serve for the lesser of two-thirds of his value and two-thirds of the kitabah price.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the mudabbir's obligation hinges on whether emancipation is divisible, with Abu Hanifa allowing choice and the Sahibayn restricting it to a fixed amount.

Ruling on Designating the Mukatab as Mudabbir
States ruling and ikhtilaf on tadbir of a mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadbir of a mukatab and explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on the choice of service when the master dies insolvent.

Core Idea
Tadbir of a mukatab is valid, but upon the master's insolvent death, Abu Hanifa grants a choice; the Sahibayn mandate the lesser amount.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a nuanced issue: what happens when a master makes his mukatab (a slave under kitabah) also a mudabbir (freed upon death). The basic ruling is that tadbir is valid because the master can immediately free the slave, so he can also suspend freedom on a condition. However, a dispute arises when the master dies insolvent and the mukatab has not become incapable. The dispute revolves around the divisibility of emancipation—a key Hanafi usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the validity of tadbir
First, note that the passage affirms the validity of designating a mukatab as mudabbir. The reason given is that the master has the power to free immediately, so he can suspend it upon a condition.
This ruling is agreed upon.
2
Understand the two outcomes if the mukatab becomes incapable
If the mukatab becomes unable to pay the kitabah (عجز), he remains a mudabbir. The tadbir takes effect because the cause for its operation exists.
3
State the scenario of ikhtilaf
The ikhtilaf arises when the mukatab does not become incapable, but the master dies insolvent (no other property). Here, Abu Hanifa gives the mukatab a choice: serve for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he must serve the lesser of the two.
The ikhtilaf is over whether the mukatab has a choice.
4
Trace the basis of the ikhtilaf
The passage states that the dispute on choice is based on whether emancipation is divisible. Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible: part of the slave's neck was freed by tadbir, part by kitabah, creating two obligations. The Sahibayn consider it indivisible, so no choice.
This was explained earlier in the text.
5
Note the agreed amount
Despite the dispute on choice, the passage notes that the amount to be served (two-thirds) is agreed upon. The reason: the kitabah price is for the entire neck; if part is freed gratis by tadbir, that portion's share drops from the kitabah.
This differs from the reverse scenario where tadbir precedes kitabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن دبر مكاتبه صح) لأنه يملك تنجيز العتق فيملك التعليق بشرط وهذا التصرف نافع له لاحتمال أن يموت المولى قبل أداء بدل الكتابة فيعتق مجاناً أو يعجز عن أداء بدل الكتابة فيبقى مدبراً قال رحمه الله : ( وإن عجز بقي مدبراً الوجود السبب الموجب له) قال رحمه الله : (وإلا سعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي البدل بموته معسراً) يعني إن لم يعجز ومات المولى معسراً فهو بالخيار بين أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي بدل الكتابة عند الإمام. وقالا : يسعى في الأقل منهما فالخلاف في الخيار مبني على تجزي الإعتاق وعدمه وقد مر بيانه . وأما المقدار هنا فمتفق عليه لأن بدل الكتابة مقابل بكل الرقبة إن لم يستحق شيء من الحرية قبل ذلك فإذا عتق بعض الرقبة مجاناً بعد ذلك سقطت حصته من بدل الكتابة بخلاف ما إذا تقدم
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If he designates his mukatab as a mudabbir, it is valid) because he has the power to immediately free him, so he has the power to suspend it upon a condition, and this action is beneficial for him since it is possible that the master may die before the payment of the kitabah price, and then he would be freed for free, or he may become incapable of paying the kitabah price and then remain a mudabbir. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he becomes incapable, he remains a mudabbir, the cause requires his existence) meaning the cause that requires him to remain mudabbir. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Otherwise, he serves for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the payment if the master dies insolvent) meaning if he does not become incapable and the master dies insolvent, he has a choice between serving for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He serves for the lesser of the two. The ikhtilaf on choice is based on the divisibility of emancipation and its non-divisibility, and its explanation has already passed. As for the amount here, there is agreement because the kitabah price is in exchange for the entire neck if nothing of freedom was previously entitled, so if some part of the neck is freed gratis afterwards, its share of the kitabah price drops, unlike if it had preceded.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of a master who designates his mukatab (a slave under kitabah) as a mudabbir (i.e., says 'you are mudabbir after my death'). The author states such tadbir is valid because the master has the right to free immediately, so he can suspend it. This benefits the slave: either the master dies before paying the kitabah price, so he is freed without payment, or if he becomes unable to pay, he remains mudabbir. The matn then says: if the mukatab becomes incapable of paying the kitabah (عجز), he remains a mudabbir. The cause for his remaining mudabbir is that the tadbir takes effect. If he does not become incapable and the master dies insolvent (no other property), then according to Abu Hanifa he has a choice between serving for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say he must serve the lesser of the two. The ikhtilaf on choice mirrors the earlier discussion based on whether emancipation is divisible (Abu Hanifa) or not (the two). However, on the amount in this scenario, there is agreement: the kitabah price is for the entire neck, so if part of the neck is freed gratis by tadbir, that portion's share of the kitabah drops. This is unlike the previous case where the mudabbir was given kitabah (in that case, the tadbir preceded, so the value of one-third was already deducted).

Key Terms
تدبير (tadbir): A master's declaration that a slave will be freed after his death.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave under kitabah contract.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave designated for deferred freedom.
عجز ('ajz): Incapacity to pay the kitabah installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does a mukatab designated as mudabbir have a choice between two-thirds of value or two-thirds of the kitabah?
A) When he becomes incapable of paying the kitabah.
B) When the master dies insolvent and he has not become incapable.
C) When the master dies with sufficient wealth to cover the kitabah.
D) When the master revokes the tadbir.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir of a mukatab is valid, but upon the master's insolvent death, the ikhtilaf on whether the slave has a choice depends on the divisibility of emancipation.

Tadbir of a Mukatab and the Dispute on Khiyar
Validity of tadbir on a mukatab and the intra-Hanafi dispute on payment upon master's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the mukatab's choice (khiyar) after tadbir when the master dies insolvent, and explain the underlying principle of divisibility of freedom (tajzi' al-'itq).

Core Idea
When a mukatab is made mudabbar and the master dies insolvent, Abu Hanifa grants a choice; Sahibayn mandate the lesser payment—all turns on whether freedom is divisible.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the validity and consequences of a master making his mukatab slave mudabbar. While the validity is agreed upon, a key intra-Hanafi dispute arises regarding the amount the mukatab must pay if the master dies before the kitabah is fulfilled. The dispute hinges on the divisibility of freedom (tajzi' al-'itq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Confirm that tadbir on a mukatab is valid according to all Hanafi imams. The master owns the slave and can attach freeing to a condition.
This is agreed upon.
2
Determine the scenario
The master dies insolvent while the mukatab is not 'unable' (i.e., he can still pay). The tadbir is in effect.
The mukatab is not unable (عجز).
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the mukatab has a choice (khiyar) between paying two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price.
Dispute is on khiyar, not the amount.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the mukatab must pay the lesser of the two amounts—no choice.
They see freedom as indivisible.
5
Uncover the root principle
The dispute is based on whether freeing is divisible (tajzi' al-'itq). Abu Hanifa says yes: tadbir frees one-third, leaving two-thirds for kitabah. Sahibayn say no: tadbir frees the entire slave, voiding the kitabah.
This is the core usul difference.
6
Practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the mukatab may choose to pay more; under Sahibayn, he always pays the lesser.
Thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن دبر مكاتبه صح لأنه يملك تنجيز العتق فيملك التعليق بشرط وهذا التصرف نافع له لاحتمال أن يموت المولى قبل أداء بدل الكتابة فيعتق مجاناً أو يعجز عن أداء بدل الكتابة فيبقى مدبراً قال رحمه الله : ( وإن عجز بقي مدير الوجود السبب الموجب له) الله : (وإلا سعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي البدل بموته معسراً) يعني إن لم يعجز ومات المولى معسراً فهو بالخيار بين أن يسعى في ثلثي قيمته أو ثلثي بدل الكتابة عند الإمام. وقالا : يسعى في الأقل منهما فالخلاف في الخيار مبني على تجزي الإعتاق وعدمه وقد مر . بيانه . وأما المقدار هنا فمتفق عليه لأن بدل الكتابة مقابل بكل الرقبة إن لم يستحق شيء من الحرية قبل ذلك فإذا عتق بعض الرقبة مجاناً بعد ذلك سقطت حصته من بدل الكتابة بخلاف ما إذا تقدم بالتدبير لأنه سلم له تدبير الثلثين فيكون بدل الكتابة مقابلاً لما لم يسلم وهو الثلث على ما . بينا .
And if he makes his mukatab mudabbar, it is valid because he owns the power to immediately free, so he owns the power to suspend it on a condition. And this action is beneficial for him because of the possibility that the master may die before payment of the kitabah price, so he will be freed for free, or he may be unable to pay the kitabah price, so he remains mudabbar. He, may God have mercy on him, said: (And if he becomes unable, he remains mudabbar with the existence of the cause that necessitates it for him.) And (Otherwise he will strive for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price upon the master's death insolvent.) Meaning that if he is not unable and the master dies insolvent, he has a choice between striving for two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two said: He strives for the lesser of the two. So the disagreement about the choice is based on the indivisibility of freeing and its absence, and its clarification has passed. As for the amount here, it is agreed upon because the kitabah price is in exchange for the entire slave's person except if some freedom was not entailed before that. So when some of the slave's person becomes free for free after that, his share of the kitabah price drops, contrary to if tadbir preceded, because he conceded the tadbir of two-thirds, so the kitabah price is in exchange for what was not conceded, which is one-third, as we explained.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the validity of a master making a tadbir (declaration that the slave will be free upon master's death) on a mukatab slave who is under a kitabah contract. The author confirms that it is valid because the master retains ownership and can attach freeing to a condition. This is beneficial for the mukatab: if the master dies before full payment, the mukatab could be freed without paying; if he becomes unable to pay, he becomes mudabbar instead of remaining in kitabah. The matn states that if the mukatab does not become unable, and the master dies insolvent, the mukatab must 'strive' (pay) two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price. Abu Hanifa holds that the mukatab has a choice between these two options. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that he must pay the lesser of the two. This intra-Hanafi dispute is based on whether freeing is divisible: Abu Hanifa sees that part of the slave is freed by tadbir (one-third) and part by kitabah, so the kitabah price is partially void; the Sahibayn see that freedom is indivisible, so the entire slave becomes free upon tadbir, voiding the kitabah entirely, leading to payment for the whole. Regarding the amount, all agree that the kitabah price is in exchange for the entire slave except for whatever freedom was already established (here one-third by tadbir), so the mukatab only pays for the remaining two-thirds. The author notes this differs from a case where tadbir preceded kitabah, where the entire price is for the remaining one-third.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered a kitabah contract with his master, whereby he earns money to pay for his freedom.
تدبير (tadbīr): A declaration by the master that the slave will be free upon the master's death (mudabbar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a master dies insolvent after making his mukatab mudabbar, according to Abu Hanifa, what is the mukatab's ruling?
A) Pay full kitabah price.
B) Pay two-thirds of his value or two-thirds of the kitabah price (choice).
C) Pay the lesser of two-thirds of value or two-thirds of kitabah.
D) Free without any payment.

Key Takeaway
The validity of tadbir on a mukatab is agreed upon, but the payment upon the master's death insolvent is disputed based on the principle of divisibility of freedom.

Freeing a Mukatab: The Ruling and Its Proof
Ruling when the master frees his mukatab without reference to kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a master independently frees his mukatab and explain the proof (dalil) from consensus.

Core Idea
When a master frees his mukatab, the slave becomes free and the kitabah debt drops—the purpose of freedom is achieved, so the payment falls away.

In this passage, the author explains a specific scenario: what happens if the master decides to free his mukatab slave outside the kitabah contract. The ruling is clear—the slave becomes free instantly and the outstanding kitabah price is canceled. This is based on the principle that ownership provides the basis for freeing, and the kitabah debt was a means to an end that has now been realized.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the master freeing his mukatab slave. The ruling: the slave becomes free and the kitabah price (badal al-kitabah) is canceled.
The text explicitly states: 'If he frees his mukatab, he becomes free and the kitabah price drops.'
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites consensus (ijma') that the kitabah contract can be dissolved by mutual consent. This is the evidence for the cancellation.
The phrase 'by consensus' (bil-ijma) is the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The consensus on dissolution by mutual consent applies here: the master's act of freeing and the slave's acceptance of freedom without payment constitute mutual consent, so the debt drops.
The master's action implies consent to dissolve, and the slave's acceptance is implicit by gaining freedom.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may require explicit consent from the slave or may not cancel the debt automatically. The Hanafi position is that mutual consent is implied by the circumstances.
This difference is recognized as legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi, supported by consensus and the reasoning that the purpose of the payment (freedom) has been achieved without it.
No intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded; the view is agreed upon within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أعتق مكاتبه عتق وسقط بدل الكتابة لأن ملكه قائم فيه وهو الشرط لنفوذ العتق . قال رحمه الله : وسقط بدل الكتابة لأن التزمه ليحصل العتق وقد حصل بدونه وكذا المولى كان يستحقه مقابلاً بالتحرير وقد فات ذلك بالإعتاق مجاناً، والكتابة وإن كانت لازمة من جانب المولى لكنها تفسخ بالتراضي الإجماع وقد وجد من المولى بالإقدام على العتق ومن العبد بحصول غرضه بلا عوض .
And if he frees his mukatab, he becomes free and the kitabah price drops because his ownership remains in him, and that is the condition for the effectiveness of freeing. He, may God have mercy on him, said: And the kitabah price drops because he undertook it to obtain freedom and it has been obtained without it. Similarly, the master was entitled to it in exchange for freeing, and that has been lost by freeing for free. And the kitabah, even if it is binding on the part of the master, is dissolved by mutual consent by consensus, and that has occurred from the master by proceeding to free and from the slave by obtaining his object without compensation.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage explains that if a master independently frees his mukatab slave (using a separate 'itq, not as part of the kitabah), the mukatab becomes free immediately and the kitabah price (the outstanding debt) is canceled. The reasoning is that the master still owns the mukatab, so his act of freeing is valid. The kitabah payment was undertaken in order to achieve freedom; now freedom is achieved without it. The master was entitled to the payment in exchange for freeing, but by freeing without compensation, that right is lost. The kitabah contract, while binding on the master, can be dissolved by mutual consent (here implied by the master's action of freeing and the slave's acceptance of freedom without payment). The author notes that this is by consensus (ijma') that the kitabah is dissolved when both parties agree to dissolve it.

Key Terms
عتق (‘itq): The act of freeing a slave by the master's voluntary declaration.
بدل الكتابة (badal al-kitābah): The price or payment agreed upon in the kitabah contract for the slave's freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A Quranic verse
B) Consensus (ijma') of the scholars
C) Analogy to freeing a regular slave
D) A hadith of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
When a master frees his mukatab, the slave becomes free instantly and the kitabah debt is canceled by implied mutual consent, as established by consensus.

Sulh on Deferred Kitabah: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on compromising the deferred kitabah price for an immediate lesser amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates sulh on deferred kitabah for immediate payment using istihsan, and distinguish it from the analogous case between free men.

Core Idea
For the mukatab, deferment is like property, so exchanging it for immediate payment is not riba.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Kitab al-Kitabah: if a master and his mukatab agree to reduce the deferred kitabah price in exchange for immediate payment, is it valid? The Hanafi school says yes, by istihsan, even though strict analogy (qiyas) would deem it riba. We will walk through the qiyas objection, the istihsan reasoning, and the limitations of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sulh (compromise) where the master accepts a lesser immediate payment in place of the deferred kitabah price. The ruling is sahih (valid) by istihsan.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
By analogy to a sulh between free men on a deferred debt, exchanging time (ajal) for a discount is riba because ajal is not property. Why does this analogy fail for the mukatab?
The asl (free men) yields invalidity; the far' (mukatab) would also be invalid by qiyas.
3
Examine the istihsan argument
For the mukatab, ajal is treated as property (mal) in one sense: he cannot pay without it. The kitabah price itself is not fully property (e.g., suretyship is invalid for it). These two factors balance, so the exchange avoids riba.
Istihsan is based on hidden consideration (ma'na khafi).
4
Note the alternative construction
The sulh can also be viewed as a dissolution (faskh) of the old kitabah and a new contract for the immediate amount, which is permissible.
This provides an additional basis for validity.
5
Recognize the limitation
This ruling is specific to kitabah. It does not apply to sulh between free men on a deferred debt, which remains invalid as riba.
The special status of the mukatab is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كاتبه على ألف مؤجلة فصالحه على نصف حال صح والقياس أن لا يجوز لأنه اعتياض عن أجل وهو ليس بمال والدين مال ولهذا لا يجوز مثله بين الحرين ولا في مكاتب الغير وإن لم يجز كان ربا وذلك في عقد المعاوضة غير جائز، وعقد المكاتبة عقد معاوضة لا ينتقض بالمهر والطلاق المقابل وبالمال. وأجيب بأن ذلك على خلاف القياس بالنص، وكذا أن تقول قوله والدين مال منقوض بقوله لو حلف بأنه ليس له مال وله دين على ملى أو معسر لم يحنث إلا أن يقال ذلك في الأيمان فتأمل. ووجه الاستحسان أن الأجل في حق المكاتب مال من وجه لأنه لا يقدر على الأداء إلا به فأعطي له حكم المال وبدل الكتابة من وجه غير مال حتى لا تصح الكفالة به فاعتدلا بخلاف العقد بين الحرين لأنه عقد من وجه فكان ربا، ولأن الصلح أمكن جعله فسخاً للكتابة السابقة وتجديد العقد على خمس مائة حالة .
And if he writes a kitabah on him for one thousand deferred, then he compromises with him for half immediately, it is valid. The analogy (qiyas) is that it is not valid because it is an exchange for time, which is not property, while debt is property. For this reason, the like is not valid between free men nor in the mukatab of another. And if it is not valid, it would be riba, and that is not permissible in a contract of exchange. The contract of kitabah is a contract of exchange that is not invalidated by (the analogy of) mahr and divorce in exchange for property. And it was answered that this is contrary to analogy by text. And likewise, you may say that his statement 'debt is property' is refuted by his statement 'if he swears that he has no property, and he has a debt from a solvent or insolvent person, he does not break his oath' unless it is said that that is in oaths, so ponder. And the basis of istihsan is that time (deferment) with respect to the mukatab is property in one sense because he cannot pay except with it, so it is given the ruling of property, while the kitabah price is in one sense not property (such that suretyship is not valid for it), so they balance. Contrary to the contract between free men, because it is a contract (of exchange) in one sense, so it becomes riba. And because the compromise can be made a dissolution of the previous kitabah and a renewal of the contract for five hundred immediately.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a master writes a kitabah for a deferred amount (e.g., 1000), and then later reaches a compromise (sulh) with the mukatab for a smaller immediate payment (e.g., 500). The author states that the ruling is that it is valid (sahih) based on istihsan, even though qiyas would prohibit it. The qiyas argument is that reducing the payment in exchange for immediate cancellation of the deferment is like exchanging time for money, which is not considered property, and thus would be riba. The author lists several points: (1) Such a transaction between free men is not valid; (2) It is not valid for a mukatab owned by another; (3) If not valid, it would be riba. However, istihsan overrides because for the mukatab, the deferment (ajal) is like property (maal) in one sense—he cannot pay without it—so it is given the legal effect of property, while the kitabah price itself is not fully property (e.g., suretyship is not valid for it). These two considerations balance, making the transaction valid. Moreover, the sulh can be viewed as a dissolution of the old kitabah and a new contract for 500 immediately, which is permissible. The author also critiques the statement 'debt is property' by noting that if one swears he has no property, while having a debt owed to him, he does not break his oath, showing that debt is not fully like property in all contexts. The istihsan ruling is specific to kitabah and does not apply to free men.

Key Terms
صلح (ṣulḥ): A compromise or settlement where one party accepts a lesser amount to settle a debt immediately.
أجل (ajal): The deferred period for payment; time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a sulh on deferred kitabah for immediate less payment valid according to istihsan?
A) Because it is exactly like sulh between free men.
B) Because for the mukatab, deferment is like property, and the kitabah price is not fully property, so the exchange balances.
C) Because it is considered a gift from the master.
D) Because the master needs the money urgently.

Key Takeaway
Sulh on deferred kitabah for immediate lesser payment is valid by istihsan because for the mukatab, deferment is treated as property, balancing the exchange.

Dispute Between Master and Mukatab on Kitabah Amount
Ruling on burden of proof in Kitabah price dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the burden of proof when a master and his mukatab differ on the amount or type of the kitabah price, and apply it to a similar dispute scenario.

Core Idea
In a Kitabah dispute, the slave's word with oath is accepted; the master must bring evidence.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common dispute in Kitabah contracts. When the master and his mukatab disagree on the price, the default rule is that the slave's statement is taken with his oath, and the master must provide evidence if he claims a higher amount. This protects the slave who is in a weaker position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and subject of dispute
The passage discusses a dispute between the master (al-mawla) and the slave (al-mukatab) regarding the kitabah price: either the amount (one thousand vs two thousand) or the type of money. This is a legal conflict over a contractual term.
In Hanafi fiqh, kitabah is a contract of manumission by payment.
2
Determine the default evidentiary rule
The judge accepts the word of the slave with his oath, because the slave is the defendant (munkir) and the master is the claimant (mudda'i) of a higher amount. The master must produce evidence (al-bayyinah) to prove his claim.
This aligns with the general Hanafi principle that the claimant must prove, and the defendant's denial is accepted with oath.
3
Apply the post-ruling scenario: later evidence
If the judge initially rules based on the slave's word and the slave pays the lower amount, but the master later brings evidence (bayyinah) for the higher amount, the ruling is revised: the slave must pay the higher amount.
The phrase 'يسعى فيهما' indicates he must work to earn and pay that amount.
4
Recognize the legal principle behind the ruling
The ruling protects the slave who is in a weaker position and cannot easily provide evidence, while still allowing the master to prove his claim if he has witnesses. This balances justice and practicality.
This is a branch (far') from the general rules of evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع : إذا اختلف المولى والعبد فقال العبد كاتبتني على ألف وقال على ألفين، أو اختلفا في جنس المال القول قول العبد مع يمينه وعلى المولى البينة وإذا جعل القاضي القول قول العبد مع يمينه وألزمه المال وأقام المولى البينة بعد ذلك على ألفين لزمه ألفان ويسعى فيهما
Branches: If the master and the slave differ, and the slave says 'You wrote kitabah on me for one thousand' and (the master) says 'for two thousand', or they differ in the type of money, the word is the word of the slave with his oath, and upon the master is the evidence (al-bayyinah). And if the judge decides that the word is the word of the slave with his oath and obligates him (to pay) the money, and then the master brings evidence for two thousand after that, then two thousand become due and he strives for them.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This short passage from the furu' (branches) gives the ruling on a dispute between a master and his mukatab regarding the amount or type of the kitabah price. The principle is that the burden of proof is on the master (the claimant of a larger amount) and the slave's statement is taken as true when he swears an oath. This is because the slave is considered to be in a weaker position and the master is the one making an additional claim. The ruling applies even if the judge initially rules based on the slave's statement (one thousand) and later the master produces evidence for two thousand; then the slave must pay the higher amount. The phrase 'ويسعى فيهما' means he works to pay that amount.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): The legal evidence, typically testimonies of two male witnesses or a male and two females.
القول قول (al-qawl qawl): The statement of a party is accepted (with oath) when there is no evidence to the contrary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The master's statement with his oath.
B) The slave's statement with his oath.
C) They split the difference.
D) The judge decides without evidence.

Key Takeaway
In a Kitabah dispute, the slave's word with oath is accepted initially; the master bears the burden of proof for a higher claim.

Sick Master's Kitaba for Excess Value: Two Hanafi Views
Explains the main ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on a sick master's kitaba for more than the slave's value, apply the analogy to khul', and evaluate the practical difference in immediate payment.

Core Idea
A sick master's kitaba for more than value: Abu Hanifa forces 2/3 of entire sum; Muhammad defers only the excess.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa with Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on the effect of a sick master's kitaba. The master dies with no other property; the slave's value is half the agreed sum. The heirs do not permit. What must the slave pay immediately? The answer differs based on whether the entire sum is considered a bequest or only the excess over value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Analyze the facts: a sick master writes a kitaba for 2000 dirhams, payable in one year, while the slave's market value is 1000 dirhams. The master dies with no other property, and the heirs do not confirm the contract. What is the slave's immediate payment obligation?
The core issue is the fate of the excess amount (1000 dirhams) and whether the entire 2000 dirhams is treated as a bequest from one-third.
2
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to the two, the slave must pay two-thirds of the entire named sum (i.e., 1333.33 dirhams) immediately, and the remaining one-third (666.67 dirhams) at the agreed term, or else return to slavery.
Their reasoning: the whole 2000 dirhams is the substitute for the slave's person (badal al-raqaba), so the heirs' rights attach to the entire amount. The muhabah (concession) is in the term, not the price.
3
State Muhammad's ruling
According to Imam Muhammad, the slave pays two-thirds of the slave's value only (i.e., 666.67 dirhams) immediately, and the entire excess (1000 dirhams) is deferred to the agreed term, or else returns to slavery.
Muhammad argues that the master could have set the kitaba at the value, so he can validly defer the increase. The muhabah is in the amount (the increase), not the term.
4
Trace Muhammad's analogy
Muhammad draws an analogy with the case of khul' (divorce initiated by wife with compensation). In khul', a sick husband can defer the compensation even without property, because the consideration is not a countervalue for property. Similarly, the excess in kitaba can be deferred.
The general principle: in marad al-mawt, concessions that are not countervalues for property are valid from the capital.
5
Examine the response of the two
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf reject the analogy with khul' because the kitaba consideration (badal al-raqaba) is directly the price for the slave's person, a property countervalue, unlike the dower in khul'. Therefore, the entire sum is subject to the one-third bequest rule.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi treatment of different contracts in marad al-mawt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (مات مريض كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة وقيمته ألف ولم تجز الورثة أدى ثلثي البدل حالاً والباقي إلى أجله أورد رقيقاً) يعني المريض إذا كاتب عبده على ألفين إلى سنة وقيمته ألف درهم فمات المولى ولا مال له غيره فإنه يؤدي ثلثي الألفين حالاً والباقي إلى أجله أو يرد رقيقاً، وهذا عند الإمام وأبي يوسف. وقال محمد يؤدي ثلثي الألف حالاً والباقي إلى أجله أو يرد رقيقاً لأن للمولى أن يترك الزيادة بأن يكاتبه على قيمته فكان له أن يؤخر الزيادة وهي ألف درهم بطريق الأولى فصار كما لو خالع المريض امرأته على ألف إلى سنة جاز، وإن لم يكن له مال آخر فصار كله مؤجلاً كما مر في باب الخلع. ولهما أن جميع المسمى بدل الرقبة حتى جرى عليه أحكام الإبدال من الأخذ بالشفعة وغيرها، وحق الورثة متعلق بالمبدل كله فكذا بالبدل بخلاف الخلع لأن البدل فيه لا يقابل المال وإن لم تتعلق الورثة بالمبدل فكذا لا تتعلق بالبلد وحاصله أن المحاباة بالأجل فيعتبر في جميع الثمن وصية من الثالث عندهما، وعنه الأجل فيما زاد على القيمة يصح من رأس المال ويعتبر في قدر القيمة الثلث.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (A sick person who writes a kitaba for his slave for two thousand [dirhams] to one year, while his value is one thousand, and the heirs do not permit, then he pays two-thirds of the consideration immediately and the remainder at its term, or he becomes a slave). Meaning: if a sick person writes a kitaba for his slave for two thousand dirhams to one year, and the slave's value is one thousand dirhams, and the master dies with no other property, then he pays two-thirds of the two thousand immediately and the remainder at its term, or he returns to slavery. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: he pays two-thirds of the one thousand immediately and the remainder at its term, or returns to slavery. Because the master had the option to forgo the increase by making the kitaba for his value, so he is able to defer the increase—which is one thousand dirhams—all the more so; thus it becomes like a sick man divorcing his wife for a deferred consideration of one thousand to a year, which is valid, even if he has no other property, so it becomes entirely deferred as passed in the chapter of khul'. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) view: the entire named [amount] is the substitute for the slave's person, so the rulings of substitution apply to it, such as pre-emption and others; and the right of the heirs attaches to the entire substituted thing, so likewise to the substitute, unlike khul' because the consideration there is not a countervalue for property, and since the heirs' right does not attach to the substituted thing, so it does not attach to the substitute. The gist is that the favorable treatment is regarding the term, so according to them it is considered a bequest from one-third in the whole price, and according to him (Muhammad?) the term regarding what exceeds the value is valid from the capital, and one-third is considered in the amount of the value.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a sick master who enters into a kitaba (contract of manumission) with his slave for more than the slave's value, and then dies without other property. The base matn states that the slave must pay two-thirds of the entire consideration immediately and the remainder at its term, or else return to slavery. The commentator explains that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad differs: he holds that only two-thirds of the slave's value (i.e., 666.67 dirhams) must be paid immediately, not two-thirds of the entire 2000. Muhammad argues by analogy: since the master could have simply written the kitaba for the value (1000), he is able to defer the extra amount by first intention (awla). He compares to the case of khul' where a deferred payment is valid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf counter that the entire named sum is the substitute for the slave's person (badal al-raqaba), so the heirs' rights attach to the whole amount, unlike khul' where the consideration is not for property. The core of the disagreement is whether the concession (muhabah) is in the amount or in the term. The commentator then notes that according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the entire price is treated as a bequest from one-third, while according to Muhammad, only the deferment beyond the value is considered from the capital and the amount equal to the value is subject to the one-third rule.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract (kitaba) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
بدل الرقبة (badal al-raqaba): The monetary consideration in a kitaba contract, considered as the substitute for the slave's person (raqaba).
محاباة (muhabah): Favorable treatment, i.e., the master giving a concession by reducing the price or deferring payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, when a sick master dies after writing a kitaba for 2000 dirhams (slave value 1000) with no other property and heirs do not permit, what must the slave pay immediately?
A) 2000 dirhams
B) 1333 dirhams
C) 667 dirhams
D) 1000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid positions on the immediate payment required from a slave in a sick master's kitaba for more than value; the relied-upon view requires payment of two-thirds of the entire named sum.
